Book of Hunting. In al-'Inayah: The appropriateness of the Book of Hunting following the Book of Beverages is that both beverages and hunting bring joy, except that beverages were placed first due to their prohibition, considering caution against them. He said in al-Muhit: It is necessary to know the permissibility of hunting, its linguistic and legal definition, its pillar, the condition for its permissibility, its proof, and the ruling of its legislation. As for the proof of permissibility from the Book: Allah's saying 'Lawful to you is the game of the sea' [5:96] and 'When you are free, then hunt' [5:2]. As for its linguistic definition: al-sayd is hunting, and it is metaphorically applied to what is hunted, by using the verbal noun for the object, and it is the wild animal that is naturally inaccessible to humans, whether edible or not. What appears is that according to jurists it is sending (al-irsal) with its conditions to take what is permissible from wild animals inaccessible to humans by their original creation. Its pillar is the taking with its conditions. Its condition related to the prey is that the prey is not secure due to ihram or the sanctum, and not owned. Its ruling is that the taken prey becomes the property of the taker. He (the author) said: 'It is hunting'. The commentator said: i.e., al-sayd is hunting in language. It is not hidden that this is not appropriate to mention in the matn so he should not have mentioned it. He said: 'And it is lawful with the trained dog, cheetah, falcon, and all other trained predators (jawarih)'. i.e., hunting is lawful with these things and other predators like the peregrine, goshawk, golden eagle, and saker. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'Anything you train from fanged beasts and clawed birds, there is no harm in hunting with it, and there is no good in what is beyond that unless you can reach its slaughter and then slaughter it.' He said in al-'Inayah: He only narrated this narration because the narration of al-Quduri indicates both proof and negation. It was objected that they explicitly stated in al-Nihayah and others that specifying something in a narration indicates negation of the ruling for what is other than it by consensus, so the narration of al-Quduri indicates proof of hunting with what we mentioned and negation of its permissibility with what is other than it, so what he mentioned is not complete. The basis for it is Allah's saying 'Lawful to you are good things and what you have taught of predators (al-jawarih)' [5:4]. Al-jawarih are those that earn, and al-jarh is earning. It is said they are those that are predatory with their fangs and claws in reality. The meaning of 'mukallibin mu'allimin' is hunting, and because in the hunting animal there is something that makes it a tool for slaughter, which is that it is predatory and cutting by nature, not rational, like a knife, and something that prevents it from being a tool for slaughter, which is that it is volitional in its action, like a human. The Law made training in it by leaving food, so it acts according to the choice of its owner, acting for him not for itself, thus becoming a pure tool for its owner like a knife. The word 'dog' applies to every beast of prey, even the lion. The second (the author?) excluded from permissibility hunting the beast of prey and the bear because they do not act for others; the lion due to its high ambition and the bear due to its baseness; thus in al-Hidayah. And in al-Nihayah they mentioned the wolf instead of the bear, and because learning is known by leaving food, and these two do not eat the prey immediately, so it is not possible to use leaving food as evidence for training. But if training could be conceived from them and known, it would be permissible; mentioned in al-Nihayah. Some annexed the kite to them due to its baseness. The pig is excluded from that because it is impure in essence. And in al-Muhit they said: Hunting with the lion and wolf is not permissible because the lion does not act for others, it only acts for itself, and the wolf is similar to it as well.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage is the opening commentary of Kitab al-Sayd in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. It begins by explaining why the Book of Hunting follows the Book of Beverages: both bring joy, but beverages were placed first due to their prohibition. Then it quotes al-Muhit on the need to understand the permissibility of hunting, its definition, pillar, conditions, proof, and ruling. The Quranic proof verses are cited: Surah al-Ma'idah 5:96 and 5:2. The linguistic definition of sayd is hunting, and it is also applied metaphorically to the game itself. The juristic definition is the sending (of an animal) with conditions to take a permissible wild animal. The pillar (rukn) is the taking with its conditions. The condition related to the prey is that it is not protected by ihram, in the Haram, or owned. The ruling is that the captured prey becomes the property of the hunter. The matn then states: 'It is hunting. And it is lawful with the trained dog, cheetah, falcon, and all other trained predators.' The commentator clarifies that 'trained predators' include shahin (peregrine), bashq (goshawk), 'uqab (eagle), and saqr (saker). He then quotes al-Jami' al-Saghir: training any fanged beast or clawed bird is permissible; what is beyond that is not unless one can slaughter it. Al-'Inayah notes that the author included this narration because al-Quduri's narration indicates both affirmation and negation. An objection follows: scholars in al-Nihayah and elsewhere agree that specifying something in a narration negates the ruling for everything else, so Quduri's narration only affirms the mentioned animals. The commentator then provides the Quranic basis (5:4) and explains that 'jawarih' means earning creatures, and the meaning of 'mukallibin mu'allimin' is 'training them for hunting'. The reasoning (qiyas) is that the hunting animal combines traits that make it a tool for slaughter (it is predatory and cuts like a knife) and traits that prevent it (it has volition). The Law makes training effective through the sign of leaving food, thereby acting on the owner's behalf like a pure tool. The word 'dog' applies to all predators, even the lion. The second (authority) excludes hunting with lion and bear because they do not act for others; the lion due to high ambition, the bear due to baseness. Al-Nihayah mentions wolf instead of bear. Training is known by the animal leaving food; lion and bear do not eat game immediately, so their leaving food cannot indicate training. However, if training could be confirmed, it would be permissible. Some add the kite due to baseness. The pig is excluded because it is inherently impure. Finally, al-Muhit states that hunting with lion and wolf is not permissible because they act only for themselves.

Key Terms
الصيد (al-sayd): Linguistically, hunting; legally, sending a trained animal to take a permissible wild animal.
الجوارح (al-jawarih): Predatory animals that earn for their owners by hunting; trained to hunt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition related to the prey for a valid hunt according to the Hanafi school?
A) The prey must be a wild animal
B) The prey must not be in ihram, in the Haram, or owned
C) The prey must be edible
D) The prey must be able to run

Key Takeaway
A valid hunt requires the prey to be unprotected by ihram or the Haram and not owned, and the animal used must be trained.

Permissible Hunting Animals and the Principle of Specification
Permissible animals and intra-Hanafi dispute on specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which animals are permissible for hunting per the Hanafi school and explain why specification in a narration negates others.

Core Idea
Only trained fanged beasts and clawed birds are permissible; specification in the text excludes all others.

In this lesson, we examine the specific animals mentioned in the matn and in al-Jami' al-Saghir for hunting. The Hanafi scholars debate whether the mention of certain animals (dog, cheetah, falcon) excludes others (like wolf, bear). You will learn the relied-upon position that specification does negate others, and understand the reasoning behind excluding certain predators like the lion and bear.

Guided Path
1
List the animals explicitly mentioned as permissible
From the matn: trained dog, cheetah, falcon, and all trained predators. From al-Jami' al-Saghir: any trained fanged beast and clawed bird.
Other predators like shahin (peregrine), bashq (goshawk), 'uqab (eagle), saqr (saker) are included under 'jawarih'.
2
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute about specification
Al-'Inayah thought Quduri's narration indicates both affirmation and negation, but the objector argues that specifying an animal in a narration (like dog, cheetah) negates permissibility for others by consensus.
This is a usul principle: takhsis (specification) implies negation of the ruling for what is not specified.
3
Identify the animals excluded and the reason
Lion and bear/wolf are excluded because they act only for themselves; the lion has high ambition, the bear is base. Training is verified by leaving food; these animals do not eat immediately, so training cannot be verified. Pig is excluded due to inherent impurity.
Some add kite due to baseness. The pig is excluded regardless of training.
4
Apply the qiyas (analogy) that makes the trained animal a tool
The trained animal cuts like a knife but has volition; the Law makes training effective through the sign of leaving food, rendering the animal a pure tool for the owner.
This analogy explains why trained animals are permissible: they act for the owner, not themselves.
5
State the mufta bihi (relied-upon ruling)
The relied-upon position is that only trained fanged beasts and clawed birds are permissible; all other animals (e.g., wolf) are not, unless one can slaughter the game conventionally.
This is the majority view, rejecting al-'Inayah's broader interpretation.

الصيد وتفسيره لغة وشرعاً وركنه وشرط إباحته ودليلها وحكم مشروعيته. أما دليل الإباحة من الكتاب قوله تعالى أحل لكم صيد البحر) [المائدة: ٩٦] وإذا حللتم فاصطادوا [المائدة: ٢] وأما تفسيره لغة فالصيد هو الإصطياد ويطلق على ما يصاد مجازاً إطلاقاً لاسم المصدر على المفعول وهو المتوحش الممتنع بأصل الخلقة عن الآدمي مأكولاً كان أو غير مأكول والذي يظهر أنه عند الفقهاء الإرسال بشروطه لأخذ ما هو مباح من الحيوان المتوحش الممتنع عن الآدمي بأصل خلقته. وأما ركنه فهو على الأخذ بشروطه. وأما شرطه المتعلق بالصيد فكون الصيد غير آمن بالإحرام والحرم وغير مملوك. وأما حكمه فصيرورة المأخوذ ملكاً للآخذ قال رحمه الله : (هو الاصطياد قال الشارح: أي الصيد هو الاصطياد في اللغة اهـ. ولا يخفى أن هذا لا يناسب أن يذكر في المتن فلا ينبغي أن يذكرها . قال رحمه الله : (ويحل بالكلب المعلم والفهد والبازي وسائر الجوارح المعلمة) يعني يحل الاصطياد بهذه الأشياء وبغيرها من الجوارح كالشاهين والباشق والعقاب والصقر. وفي الجامع الصغير : وكل شيء علمته من ذي ناب من السباع وذي مخلب من الطير فلا بأس بصيده ولا خير فيما سوى ذلك إلا أن تدرك ذكاته فتذكيه قال في العناية وإنما أورد هذه الرواية لأن رواية القدوري تدل على الإثبات والنفي جميعاً .اهـ. واعترض بأنهم قد صرحوا في النهاية وغيرها بأن تخصيص الشيء بالذكر في الرواية يدل على نفي الحكم عما عداه بالاتفاق، فرواية القدوري تدل على إثبات الصيد بما ذكرنا ونفي جوازه بما سواه فلم يتم ما ذكره، والأصل فيه قوله تعالى أحل لكم الطيبات وما علمتم من الجوارح﴾ [المائدة: ٤] والجوارح الكواسب والجرح الكسب . وقيل هي أن تكون جارحة بنابها ومخلبها حقيقة. ومعنى مكلبين معلمين الاصطياد ولأنه اجتمع في الحيوان الصائد ما يوجب أن يكون آلة للذبح وهو كونه جارحاً قاطعاً بطبعه غير عاقل كالسكين وما يمنع أن يكون آلة للذبح وهو كونه مختاراً في فعله كالآدمي والشرع جعل التعليم فيه بترك الأكل فيجري على موجب اختيار صاحبه فيعمل له لا لنفسه فيصير آلة محضة لصاحبه كالسكين واسم الكلب يقع على كل سبع حتى الأسد، واستثنى الثاني من الجواز اصطياد السبع والذب لأنهما لا يعملان لغيرهما؛ الأسد لعلو همته والدب لخساسته ؛ كذا في الهداية. وذكر في النهاية الذئب بدل الدب ولأن التعلم يعرف بترك الأكل وهما لا يأكلان الصيد في الحال فلا يمكن الاستدلال بترك الأكل على التعليم حتى لو تصور التعليم منهما وعرف ذلك جاز؛ ذكره في النهاية. وألحق بعضهم الحدأة بهما لخساستها. والخنزير مستثنى من ذلك لأنه نجس العين. وفي المحيط قالوا: لا يجوز الاصطياد بالأسد والذئب لأن الأسد لا يعمل لغيره وإنما يعمل لنفسه، والذئب مثله أن أيضاً.
Book of Hunting. In al-'Inayah: The appropriateness of the Book of Hunting following the Book of Beverages is that both beverages and hunting bring joy, except that beverages were placed first due to their prohibition, considering caution against them. He said in al-Muhit: It is necessary to know the permissibility of hunting, its linguistic and legal definition, its pillar, the condition for its permissibility, its proof, and the ruling of its legislation. As for the proof of permissibility from the Book: Allah's saying 'Lawful to you is the game of the sea' [5:96] and 'When you are free, then hunt' [5:2]. As for its linguistic definition: al-sayd is hunting, and it is metaphorically applied to what is hunted, by using the verbal noun for the object, and it is the wild animal that is naturally inaccessible to humans, whether edible or not. What appears is that according to jurists it is sending (al-irsal) with its conditions to take what is permissible from wild animals inaccessible to humans by their original creation. Its pillar is the taking with its conditions. Its condition related to the prey is that the prey is not secure due to ihram or the sanctum, and not owned. Its ruling is that the taken prey becomes the property of the taker. He (the author) said: 'It is hunting'. The commentator said: i.e., al-sayd is hunting in language. It is not hidden that this is not appropriate to mention in the matn so he should not have mentioned it. He said: 'And it is lawful with the trained dog, cheetah, falcon, and all other trained predators (jawarih)'. i.e., hunting is lawful with these things and other predators like the peregrine, goshawk, golden eagle, and saker. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'Anything you train from fanged beasts and clawed birds, there is no harm in hunting with it, and there is no good in what is beyond that unless you can reach its slaughter and then slaughter it.' He said in al-'Inayah: He only narrated this narration because the narration of al-Quduri indicates both proof and negation. It was objected that they explicitly stated in al-Nihayah and others that specifying something in a narration indicates negation of the ruling for what is other than it by consensus, so the narration of al-Quduri indicates proof of hunting with what we mentioned and negation of its permissibility with what is other than it, so what he mentioned is not complete. The basis for it is Allah's saying 'Lawful to you are good things and what you have taught of predators (al-jawarih)' [5:4]. Al-jawarih are those that earn, and al-jarh is earning. It is said they are those that are predatory with their fangs and claws in reality. The meaning of 'mukallibin mu'allimin' is hunting, and because in the hunting animal there is something that makes it a tool for slaughter, which is that it is predatory and cutting by nature, not rational, like a knife, and something that prevents it from being a tool for slaughter, which is that it is volitional in its action, like a human. The Law made training in it by leaving food, so it acts according to the choice of its owner, acting for him not for itself, thus becoming a pure tool for its owner like a knife. The word 'dog' applies to every beast of prey, even the lion. The second (the author?) excluded from permissibility hunting the beast of prey and the bear because they do not act for others; the lion due to its high ambition and the bear due to its baseness; thus in al-Hidayah. And in al-Nihayah they mentioned the wolf instead of the bear, and because learning is known by leaving food, and these two do not eat the prey immediately, so it is not possible to use leaving food as evidence for training. But if training could be conceived from them and known, it would be permissible; mentioned in al-Nihayah. Some annexed the kite to them due to its baseness. The pig is excluded from that because it is impure in essence. And in al-Muhit they said: Hunting with the lion and wolf is not permissible because the lion does not act for others, it only acts for itself, and the wolf is similar to it as well.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage is the opening commentary of Kitab al-Sayd in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. It begins by explaining why the Book of Hunting follows the Book of Beverages: both bring joy, but beverages were placed first due to their prohibition. Then it quotes al-Muhit on the need to understand the permissibility of hunting, its definition, pillar, conditions, proof, and ruling. The Quranic proof verses are cited: Surah al-Ma'idah 5:96 and 5:2. The linguistic definition of sayd is hunting, and it is also applied metaphorically to the game itself. The juristic definition is the sending (of an animal) with conditions to take a permissible wild animal. The pillar (rukn) is the taking with its conditions. The condition related to the prey is that it is not protected by ihram, in the Haram, or owned. The ruling is that the captured prey becomes the property of the hunter. The matn then states: 'It is hunting. And it is lawful with the trained dog, cheetah, falcon, and all other trained predators.' The commentator clarifies that 'trained predators' include shahin (peregrine), bashq (goshawk), 'uqab (eagle), and saqr (saker). He then quotes al-Jami' al-Saghir: training any fanged beast or clawed bird is permissible; what is beyond that is not unless one can slaughter it. Al-'Inayah notes that the author included this narration because al-Quduri's narration indicates both affirmation and negation. An objection follows: scholars in al-Nihayah and elsewhere agree that specifying something in a narration negates the ruling for everything else, so Quduri's narration only affirms the mentioned animals. The commentator then provides the Quranic basis (5:4) and explains that 'jawarih' means earning creatures, and the meaning of 'mukallibin mu'allimin' is 'training them for hunting'. The reasoning (qiyas) is that the hunting animal combines traits that make it a tool for slaughter (it is predatory and cuts like a knife) and traits that prevent it (it has volition). The Law makes training effective through the sign of leaving food, thereby acting on the owner's behalf like a pure tool. The word 'dog' applies to all predators, even the lion. The second (authority) excludes hunting with lion and bear because they do not act for others; the lion due to high ambition, the bear due to baseness. Al-Nihayah mentions wolf instead of bear. Training is known by the animal leaving food; lion and bear do not eat game immediately, so their leaving food cannot indicate training. However, if training could be confirmed, it would be permissible. Some add the kite due to baseness. The pig is excluded because it is inherently impure. Finally, al-Muhit states that hunting with lion and wolf is not permissible because they act only for themselves.

Key Terms
الجوارح (al-jawarih): Predatory animals that earn for their owners; trained to hunt. Includes dog, cheetah, falcon, etc.
التعليم (al-ta'lim): Training the hunting animal so that it responds to command and leaves the prey uneaten.
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification; limiting a general ruling to specific instances mentioned in the text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, why is hunting with a trained wolf not permissible?
A) Because wolves are impure
B) Because wolves cannot be trained
C) Because the wolf is not among the specified animals in the narration
D) Because wolves always eat their prey

Key Takeaway
Only trained fanged beasts and clawed birds are permissible for hunting; specification in the text excludes all other animals.

The Fifteen Conditions for Lawful Hunting in Hanafi Fiqh
Enumeration of fifteen conditions with critical refinement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fifteen conditions for lawful hunting and explain why the condition of death before slaughter is distinct from killing by injury.

Core Idea
Hunting is only lawful if all fifteen conditions are met; missing any condition requires proper slaughter if the animal is caught alive.

Al-Khulasah presents a comprehensive list of fifteen conditions that must be fulfilled for hunting to be lawful in the Hanafi school. These conditions are divided into three categories related to the hunter, the hunting dog, and the prey. A later critical objection questioned whether the condition that the prey dies before the hunter reaches it is redundant with the condition that the dog kills by injury. The response clarifies that they serve distinct purposes, which this lesson will unpack.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five hunter conditions
List the conditions pertaining to the one who sends the hunting animal: eligibility for slaughter, actual sending, no sharing of sending with another whose hunt is lawful, no intentional omission of tasmiyah, and no extraneous action between sending and taking.
These conditions ensure the hunter's intent and eligibility.
2
Identify the five dog conditions
List the conditions for the hunting animal: it must be trained, go in the direction sent, no sharing with someone whose hunt is not lawful, kill by injury (not strangulation), and not eat from the prey.
The dog must be acting as a tool for the hunter, not for itself.
3
Identify the five prey conditions
List the conditions regarding the game: it must not rely on fangs or claws, not be an insect, not be aquatic except fish, be able to defend itself, and die from the wound before the hunter reaches it to slaughter.
These conditions exclude certain animals and define the required mode of death.
4
Analyse the objection about redundancy
Examine the objection that the condition 'dies before the hunter reaches' is repetitive after 'kills by injury'. Understand the objection and its basis.
The objector viewed the two conditions as having the same effect.
5
Understand the distinction and response
Learn why the conditions are distinct: 'kills by injury' ensures the kill is not by strangulation; 'dies before the hunter reaches' handles the case where the dog wounds the prey after the hunter is present, requiring tadhkiyah. The conditions are for pure hunting (where the animal is not caught alive); if caught alive, tadhkiyah is required.
This clarifies the scope of the conditions.

قال الخلاصة: وإنما يحل الصيد بخمسة عشر شرطاً؛ خمسة في في يكون من أهل الذكاة، وأن يوجد منه الإرسال ولا يشاركه في الإرسال من يحل صيده . وأن لا يترك التسمية عمداً، ولا يشتغل بين الإرسال والأخذ بعمل. وخمسة في الكلب منها الأخذ أن يكون معلماً، وأن يذهب على سنن الإرسال، وأن لا يشاركه في من لا يحل صيده، وأن يقتله جرحاً، وأن لا يأكل منه . وخمسة في الصيد منها أن لا يكون متقوياً بأنيابه أو بمخلبه وأن لا يكون من الحشرات وأن لا يكون من بنات الماء سوی السمك، وأن يمنع نفسه بجناحة أو مخلبه، وأن يموت بهذا قبل أن يصل إلى ذبحه اهـ. وذكر صاحب النهاية والعناية وغاية البيان نقلاً عن الخلاصة واعترض بأن قوله وأن يموت قبل أن يصل إلى ذبحه مستدرك بعد قوله وأن يقتله جرحاً». وأجيب بأن لا استدراك لأن الشرط الذي أريد بقولة وأن يقتله جرحاً ليس مجرد قتله بل قتله جرحاً والمقصود منه الاحتراز عن قتله خنقاً. والشرط الذي أريد بقوله وأن يموت بهذا قبل أن يصل إلى ذبحه» لجواز أن يقتله الكلب جرحاً بعد أن يصل المرسل إلى ذبحه فحينئذ لا يحل أكله فلا بد من بيان الشرط الآخر أيضاً على الاستقلال. قال صاحب العناية : فيما نقله صاحب الخلاصة تسامح لأن هذا شرط الاصطياد للأكل بالكلب لا غيره على أنه لو انتقى بعضه لم يحرم كما لو اشتغل بعمل غيره لكن أدركه حياً ،فذبحه وكذا لو لم يمت بهذا لكن ذبحه فإنه صيد وهو حلال اهـ. وأجيب بأن هذه الشروط في الصيد المحض وهو الذي لم يدركه حياً، أما الذي أدركه فذكاه بالذكاة الاختيارية فليس صيداً محضاً بل يلحق به .اهـ. والمراد بقول صاحب العناية شرط الاصطياد أي حال الاصطياد وفي التعبير بما يدل على ظهور المراد لا يبالي بمثله. قال رحمه الله: (ولا
Al-Khulasah said: Hunting is only lawful with fifteen conditions: five related to the hunter: he must be one who is eligible for slaughter (tadhkiyah), that his sending (irsal) occurs, and no one whose hunt is permissible shares in the sending, and that he does not intentionally omit the tasmiyah (Bismillah), and he does not engage in any other action between sending and taking. Five conditions related to the dog: it must be trained, it goes according to the direction of sending, no one whose hunt is not permissible shares with it, it kills by injury (jarh), and it does not eat from the prey. Five conditions related to the prey: it is not one that relies on its fangs or claws, it is not from insects (hasharat), it is not from aquatic animals except fish, it defends itself with its wings or claws, and it dies by this before the hunter reaches it to slaughter it. The author of al-Nihayah and al-'Inayah and Ghayat al-Bayan quoted from al-Khulasah and objected that his saying 'and it dies by this before the hunter reaches to slaughter it' is repetitive after his saying 'and it kills by injury'. It was answered that there is no repetition because the condition intended by 'and it kills by injury' is not mere killing but killing by injury, and the purpose is to avoid killing by strangulation. The condition intended by 'and it dies by this before the hunter reaches to slaughter it' is for the possibility that the dog kills by injury after the sender reaches it to slaughter it; then it would not be lawful to eat it, so the other condition must also be stated independently. The author of al-'Inayah said: In what the author of al-Khulasah narrated, there is an approximation because this is a condition of hunting for eating with the dog specifically; if some of them are missing, it is not prohibited, as if it engaged in other action but he caught it alive and slaughtered it, and likewise if it did not die by this but he slaughtered it, then it is game and is lawful. It was answered that these conditions are for pure hunting (al-sayd al-mahd), which is what one does not catch alive; as for what one catches alive, he slaughters it with optional slaughter, so it is not pure hunting but is attached to it. The intention of the saying of the author of al-'Inayah that 'condition of hunting' means the state of hunting, and in the expression that indicates the appearance of the intended meaning, one does not care about such an expression. He (the author) said: 'And not...'
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage enumerates the fifteen conditions for lawful hunting as transmitted from al-Khulasah, though the text cuts off at the end. The conditions are divided into three categories: five related to the hunter, five to the dog, and five to the prey. The hunter conditions include being a person eligible to perform tadhkiyah (slaughter), sending the animal himself without sharing the sending with someone whose hunt is lawful, not intentionally omitting the tasmiyah (saying Bismillah), and not engaging in any unrelated action between sending and taking. The dog conditions are that it must be trained (mu'allam), it proceeds in the direction it was sent, no one whose hunt is not permissible (e.g., an idolater) shares in the sending, it kills by wounding (not by strangulation), and it does not eat from the prey. The prey conditions are that it does not rely on its fangs or claws (like predators), it is not an insect, it is not aquatic except fish, it defends itself with its wings or claws (i.e., it is able to escape), and it dies from the wound before the hunter reaches it to slaughter it. The text then records an objection from the commentators of al-Nihayah, al-'Inayah, and Ghayat al-Bayan: the condition 'it dies before the hunter reaches to slaughter it' seems redundant after 'it kills by injury'. The response clarifies that the two conditions are distinct: the first ensures the kill is by injury (not strangulation), the second ensures the death occurs before the hunter reaches it, because if the dog wounds it but the hunter reaches it alive, it must be slaughtered by tadhkiyah; if it dies after the hunter reaches it, it is not considered game. Al-'Inayah criticizes the conditions as being an approximation, arguing that they apply only to hunting for food with a dog, and if some condition is missing, it does not render the meat unlawful if the animal is caught alive and slaughtered. The response maintains that the conditions are for pure hunting (where the animal is not caught alive); if caught alive, tadhkiyah is required. The passage ends mid-sentence at the matn's continuation.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Uttering 'Bismillah' at the time of sending the hunting animal.
الإرسال (al-irsal): The act of sending the trained animal towards the prey.
الذكاة (al-tadhkiyah): Ritual slaughter according to Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Lawful hunting in the Hanafi school requires fifteen conditions across the hunter, dog, and prey; the key nuance is that the prey must die from the wound before the hunter reaches it, or else proper slaughter is necessary.

Obligation of Tasmiya and Location of the Wound in Hunting
Ruling on saying Bismillah at release and that the wound can be anywhere on the prey's body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the necessity of tasmiya when releasing a hunting animal and explain that the wound can be on any part of the prey's body, citing the Quranic proof and hadith.

Core Idea
Saying Bismillah at release is wajib for hunting; the wound can be anywhere on the prey.

In this passage, Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies two key conditions for the permissibility of hunting: the hunter must say 'Bismillah' at the moment of releasing the dog or falcon, and the resulting wound can be on any part of the prey's body—not just the neck as in slaughter. The ruling is based on the Quranic verse 'Do not eat of that over which the name of Allah has not been mentioned' and the hadith of Abu Tha'laba. The text also addresses a special case for fish and discusses how to determine if a hunting animal is trained.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, identify the act being ruled upon: hunting with a trained dog or falcon. The ruling is that tasmiya (saying Bismillah) at the moment of release is wajib, and the wound can be anywhere on the prey's body.
The act is the irsal (release), and the ruling includes both an obligation (tasmiya) and a condition (wound location).
2
Locate the proof
The author cites two proofs: Quran 6:121 (prohibition of eating without mentioning Allah's name) and the hadith narrated by Abu Tha'laba where the Prophet said: 'If you mention Allah's name and it wounds, then eat.'
The Quranic verse is general; the hadith specifies it for hunting.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition in the verse implies that mentioning Allah's name is a condition for permissibility. The hadith explicitly connects tasmiya with the wound, establishing that the wound need not be in a specific spot.
The phrase 'وَجَرَحَ' (and it wounds) indicates that any wound suffices, not necessarily in a particular location.
4
Note the exception for fish
The author states that the requirement of tasmiya does not apply to fish, based on a distinction: fish are not considered 'said' in the same way as land animals. If one intentionally omits tasmiya when aiming at fish, the catch is still halal.
This is an exception to the general rule; the text says 'لو رمى إلى السمك وترك التسمية عمداً فأصاب يحل أكله'.
5
Evaluate the training discussion
The passage also repeats earlier discussion on what constitutes a trained animal. For dogs, training is established by leaving food three times; for falcons, by returning when called. This is an intra-Hanafi point with some difference on the number of times, but the relied-upon position is three.
This part of the passage is tangential to the main ruling but shows the complexity of defining 'mu'allam' (trained).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التسمية عند الإرسال ومن الجرح في أي كان موضع من أعضائه فإن أكل منه البازي بد من التعليم لقوله تعالى ﴿وما علمتم من الجوارح مكلبين تعلمونهن﴾ [المائدة: ٤] ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لأبي ثعلبة ما صدت بكلبك المعلم فذكرت اسم الله عليه فكل وما صدت بكلبك غير المعلم فأدركت ذكاته فكل رواه البخاري ومسلم وأحمد. ولذا لا بد أن يكون المرسل أهلاً للذكاة بأن يكون مسلماً أو كتابياً ويعقل التسمية ويضبط على نحو ما ذكرنا في الذبائح . قال رحمه الله : (وإذا ترك الأكل ثلاثاً في الكلب وبالرجوع إذا دعوته في البازي) أي التعليم في الكلب يكون بترك الأكل ثلاث مرات، وفي البازي في الرجوع إذا دعي. روي ذلك عن ابن عباس رضي الله تعالى عنهما. ولأن بدن الكلب يحتمل الضرب فيمكن ضربه حتى يترك الأكل وبدن البازي لا يحتمل الضرب فلا يمكن تحقيق هذا الشرط فيه فاكتفي بغيره مما يدل على التعليم ولأن آية التعليم ترك ما هو مألوفة عادة وعادة البازي التوحش والاستنفاد وعادة الكلب الانتهاب والاستلاب لائتلافه بالناس فإذا ترك كل واحد منهما مألوفة دل على تعليمه وانتهاء علمه وهذا الفرق لا يتأتى إلا في الكلب خاصة لأنه هو الألوف دون غيره من ذوات الأنياب فإنها ليست بألوفة والفرق الأول يتأتى في الكل لأن بدن كل ذي ناب يحتمل الضرب فأمكن تعليمه بالضرب إلى أن يترك الأكل. قال صاحب النهاية : وهذا الفرق لا يتأتى في الفهد والنمر فإنه متوحش كالباز . ثم الحكم فيه وفي الكلب سواء فالمعتمد هو الأول؛ كذا في المبسوط وأجيب بأن الكلب في اللغة يقع على كل سبع، وليس المراد مما ذكره المؤلف الكلب المعهود بل الكلب بالمعنى اللغوي فلهذا استووا فيما يقع به التعليم وإنما شرط ترك الأكل ثلاث مرات وهو قولهما ورواية عن أبي حنيفة رضي الله تعالى عنه لأن علمه يعرف بتكرار التجارب والامتحان هو مدة ضربت لذلك كما في قصة السيد موسى وكما في شرط الخيار، وكذا قال : إذا استأذن أحدكم ثلاثاً فلم يؤذن له فليرجع». وعن الإمام أنه لم يثبت التعليم ما لم يغلب على ظنه أنه قد تعلم ولا يقدر بشيء لأن المقادير تعرف بالنص لا بالاجتهاد لا نص هنا فيفوض إلى رأي المبتلي كما هو إذا ترك الأكل ثلاثاً لا يحل الأول ولا الثاني على قول من قال بالثلاث، وكذا الثالث عندهما معلماً إلا بعد تمام الثلاث وقبله غير معلم. قال رحمه الله : (ولا بد من التسمية عند الإرسال ومن الجرح في أي موضع كان من أعضائه أما التسمية لقوله تعالى: ﴿ولا تأكلوا مما لم يذكر اسم الله عليه ﴾ [الأنعام: ۱۲۱] ولقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «فإذا ذكرت الله تعالى عليه وجرح فكل وأطلق في قوله ولا بد من التسمية فشمل ما إذا كان المرمى إليه يحتاج إلى التسمية أو لا كالسمك، وقد شرط في الأول دون الثاني حتى لو رمى إلى السمك وترك التسمية عمداً فأصاب يحل أكله، فلو قال في صيد البر لكان أولى وسيأتي عن قاضيخان. ولا
The naming at release and the wound in any part of its limbs. If the falcon eats from it... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, stating that saying Bismillah (tasmiya) at the time of releasing the hunting animal is obligatory, and the wound that kills the prey can be anywhere on its body, not necessarily in a specific spot. The proof is from the Quranic verse 'Do not eat of that over which the name of Allah has not been mentioned' and the hadith of Abu Tha'laba where the Prophet said: 'If you mention Allah's name and it wounds, then eat.' The author notes that this requirement applies to all hunting, including land animals, but there is a nuance regarding fish: if one shoots an arrow at fish and forgets tasmiya intentionally, the catch is still halal because fish do not require tasmiya. The passage then repeats the discussion on teaching from the previous lesson, clarifying that the dog's teaching is by leaving food three times and the falcon's by returning when called, with an intra-Hanafi difference of opinion on the number. The relied-upon position is that three times are necessary.

Key Terms
تسمية (tasmiya): Saying 'Bismillahi Allahu Akbar' or similar at the time of releasing the hunting animal.
جرح (jarh): The wound inflicted by the hunting animal; it can be on any part of the prey's body.
إرسال (irsal): The act of releasing the hunting animal to chase the prey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hunter shoots an arrow at a fish but forgets to say Bismillah intentionally, is the fish halal to eat according to the Hanafi school as per this text?
A) Yes, because fish do not require tasmiya.
B) No, because tasmiya is obligatory for all hunting.
C) Yes, because the intention was to hunt.
D) No, because forgetting intentionally invalidates the catch.

Key Takeaway
Tasmiya at release is wajib for land game, but fish are an exception; the wound can be anywhere on the prey's body.

Condition of Training (Ta'lim) for Hunting Animals
Defines training criteria with proofs and intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi criteria for a hunting animal being considered mu'allam, distinguish between dog and hawk, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on quantification.

Core Idea
Training (ta'lim) is essential for halal hunting; dog leaves food three times, hawk returns when called, but quantification is debated.

Hunting with trained animals is permissible in Islam, but the animal must be properly trained (mu'allam) to ensure the prey is halal without slaughter. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the specific criteria for dogs and birds of prey, citing Quranic and prophetic proofs, and then navigates an important intra-Hanafi disagreement about whether the number of training attempts is strictly fixed or left to the trainer's judgment. By understanding these conditions, you will be able to evaluate the permissibility of hunting scenarios in daily life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall ruling and its proofs
Recognize that training (ta'lim) is a necessary condition (wajib) for the permissibility of eating prey caught by a hunting animal. Note the Quranic verse (5:4) and the hadith of Abu Tha'labah as the primary evidence.
The hadith explicitly distinguishes between trained and untrained dogs.
2
Extract the specific criteria for dog and hawk
Observe that for a dog, training is established by leaving food three times; for a hawk, by returning when called. Understand the reasoning: dogs can be beaten to break their habit, hawks cannot, so different indicators are needed.
The criteria are based on the animal's natural behavior and physical capacity.
3
Analyze the reasoning behind the different criteria
Follow the text's explanation: 'dog' linguistically includes all predators, but the physical distinction (ability to endure beating) justifies different tests. The author also cites a narration from Ibn Abbas.
The cheetah and leopard are treated like the hawk due to their wild nature.
4
Map the intra-Hanafi dispute on quantification
Identify the two positions: (1) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (and a narration from Abu Hanifa) require three refusals as a fixed measure. (2) Another narration from Abu Hanifa leaves it to the trainer's dominant presumption, with no fixed number.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the unquantified view according to al-Mabsut.
5
Determine the practical thamarah (consequence)
Consider the difference: If three times is required, the dog is considered untrained until after the third refusal; the prey caught before that is not halal. If unquantified, the trainer's judgment determines when the dog is trained.
The mufta bihi leaves flexibility for the trainer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بد من التعليم لقوله تعالى وما علمتم من الجوارح مكلبين تعلمونهن ﴾ [المائدة: ٤] ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لأبي ثعلبة ما صدت بكلبك المعلم فذكرت اسم الله عليه فكل وما صدت بكلبك غير المعلم فأدركت ذكاته فكل رواه البخاري ومسلم وأحمد. ولذا لا بد أن يكون المرسل أهلاً للذكاة بأن يكون مسلماً أو كتابياً ويعقل التسمية ويضبط على نحو ما ذكرنا في الذبائح . قال رحمه الله : (وإذا ترك الأكل ثلاثاً في الكلب وبالرجوع إذا دعوته في البازي) أي التعليم في الكلب يكون بترك الأكل ثلاث مرات، وفي البازي في الرجوع إذا دعي. روي ذلك عن ابن عباس رضي الله تعالى عنهما. ولأن بدن الكلب يحتمل الضرب فيمكن ضربه حتى يترك الأكل وبدن البازي لا يحتمل الضرب فلا يمكن تحقيق هذا الشرط فيه فاكتفي بغيره مما يدل على التعليم ولأن آية التعليم ترك ما هو مألوفة عادة وعادة البازي التوحش والاستنفاد وعادة الكلب الانتهاب والاستلاب لائتلافه بالناس فإذا ترك كل واحد منهما مألوفة دل على تعليمه وانتهاء علمه وهذا الفرق لا يتأتى إلا في الكلب خاصة لأنه هو الألوف دون غيره من ذوات الأنياب فإنها ليست بألوفة والفرق الأول يتأتى في الكل لأن بدن كل ذي ناب يحتمل الضرب فأمكن تعليمه بالضرب إلى أن يترك الأكل. قال صاحب النهاية : وهذا الفرق لا يتأتى في الفهد والنمر فإنه متوحش كالباز . ثم الحكم فيه وفي الكلب سواء فالمعتمد هو الأول؛ كذا في المبسوط وأجيب بأن الكلب في اللغة يقع على كل سبع، وليس المراد مما ذكره المؤلف الكلب المعهود بل الكلب بالمعنى اللغوي فلهذا استووا فيما يقع به التعليم وإنما شرط ترك الأكل ثلاث مرات وهو قولهما ورواية عن أبي حنيفة رضي الله تعالى عنه لأن علمه يعرف بتكرار التجارب والامتحان هو مدة ضربت لذلك كما في قصة السيد موسى وكما في شرط الخيار، وكذا قال : إذا استأذن أحدكم ثلاثاً فلم يؤذن له فليرجع». وعن الإمام أنه لم يثبت التعليم ما لم يغلب على ظنه أنه قد تعلم ولا يقدر بشيء لأن المقادير تعرف بالنص لا بالاجتهاد لا نص هنا فيفوض إلى رأي المبتلي كما هو إذا ترك الأكل ثلاثاً لا يحل الأول ولا الثاني على قول من قال بالثلاث، وكذا الثالث عندهما معلماً إلا بعد تمام الثلاث وقبله غير معلم.
Training is necessary, due to the Almighty's saying: 'And what you have taught of hunting animals...' [al-Ma'idah:4] and His saying, peace be upon him, to Abu Tha'labah: 'What you hunt with your trained dog, and you mention Allah's name over it, eat; and what you hunt with your untrained dog, and you reach it still alive, slaughter it and eat' narrated by Bukhari, Muslim, and Ahmad. Hence the releaser must be qualified for slaughter, i.e., Muslim or Kitabi, and understanding of tasmiyah, and precise as we mentioned in the chapter of slaughter. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And [training is] by leaving food three times for the dog, and by returning when called for the hawk). That is, training for the dog is by leaving food three times, and for the hawk by returning when called. This is narrated from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both. Because the dog's body can withstand beating, so it can be beaten until it leaves food, whereas the hawk's body cannot withstand beating, so this condition cannot be realized in it, so another indication of training suffices. And because the verse of training is abandoning what is customary, and the hawk's habit is wildness and flight, while the dog's habit is grabbing and plundering due to its familiarity with people. So when each abandons its habit, it indicates its training and knowledge. This distinction only applies to the dog specifically, as it is familiar, unlike other canines which are not familiar. The first distinction applies to all, because the body of every canine can withstand beating, so training can be achieved by beating until it leaves food. The author of al-Nihayah said: This distinction does not apply to the cheetah and leopard, as they are wild like the hawk. Then the ruling is the same for them and the dog, so the relied-upon is the first opinion; as in al-Mabsut. And it was answered that 'dog' linguistically includes every predator, and the author's intent is not the specific dog but the linguistic meaning, so they are equal in what constitutes training. And the condition of leaving food three times is the opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and a narration from Abu Hanifa, because its knowledge is known by repeated trials, and the test is a period set for that, as in the story of Sayyiduna Musa, and as in the condition of option. Likewise, he said: 'If one of you asks permission three times and is not permitted, let him return.' And from the Imam (Abu Hanifa) that training is not confirmed unless it becomes his dominant presumption that it has learned, and it is not quantified by anything, because measures are known by text, not by ijtihad, and there is no text here, so it is left to the judgment of the tester. Thus, if it leaves food three times, the first and second are not permissible according to those who say three, and likewise the third according to them is not trained until after the completion of three, and before that it is untrained.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the condition of training (تعليم) for hunting animals. The text first establishes that training is a necessary condition, citing Quran and Hadith. Then it defines the specific criteria: for dogs, training is demonstrated by leaving food three times; for hawks, by returning when called. The reasoning is based on the animal's physical capacity to be beaten and its natural habits. There is a intra-Hanafi dispute: the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to al-Mabsut is that training is not strictly quantified by three times but depends on the trainer's dominant presumption. However, the text also presents the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad that three times is the standard. The passage concludes that the third kill immediately after the third refusal is not considered trained until after completion of the three refusals.

Key Terms
تعليم (ta'lim): Training of a hunting animal such that it obeys commands and refrains from its natural predatory habits (e.g., dog leaves food, hawk returns when called).
معلم (mu'allam): A trained hunting animal that has been taught to hunt and obey, as per the criteria in this passage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how is a dog considered trained (mu'allam) for hunting?
A) By being beaten until it stops eating prey
B) By leaving food three times
C) By returning when called
D) By being muzzled

Key Takeaway
Training (ta'lim) is a necessary condition for a hunting animal; the criteria differ for dogs and hawks, and the Hanafi school largely leaves quantification to the trainer's judgment.

Obligation of Tasmiyah at Release
Ruling with proof and exceptions for tasmiyah in hunting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tasmiyah at release, identify the evidence from Quran and Hadith, and apply the exceptions for fishing, insane persons, mute, Kitabi, and invalid tasmiyah.

Core Idea
Tasmiyah is wajib at release for land hunting; deliberate omission makes the prey haram, but fishing is exempt.

This lesson examines the obligation of tasmiyah (saying 'Bismillah') when releasing a hunting animal. The Hanafi school requires it based on clear textual evidence, but with important exceptions that affect the permissibility of the prey. We will work through the proof, the conditions, and the edge cases detailed in the passage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the hukm (obligation level) is according to the Hanafi school.
The act is releasing a hunting animal; the ruling is that tasmiyah is necessary (wajib).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence cited: Quran 6:121 and the Hadith. Understand they are used to prove the obligation.
Quran: 'Do not eat of that upon which Allah's name has not been mentioned'; Hadith: 'If you mention Allah over it and it wounds, then eat.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the dalil leads to the ruling. The Quranic prohibition implies that mentioning Allah's name is required, and the Hadith conditions eating on mentioning Allah's name.
The imperative to mention Allah's name is taken as an obligation (wajib) in Hanafi usul.
4
Identify exceptions and conditions
Note the specific exceptions: fishing (no tasmiyah needed), insane (if they don't understand), mute and Kitabi (millah suffices), and Christian tasmiyah in Christ's name (invalid).
Also note the requirement that the releaser must be sane and the prey must be wounded.
5
Apply to scenarios
Use the framework to determine the permissibility of prey in various cases, e.g., deliberate omission, forgetfulness, hunting with a dog, etc.
Practice with the practice tasks.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا بد من التسمية عند الإرسال ومن الجرح في أي موضع كان من أعضائه) أما التسمية لقوله تعالى: ﴿ولا تأكلوا مما لم يذكر اسم الله عليه ﴾ [الأنعام: ۱۲۱] ولقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «فإذا ذكرت الله تعالى عليه وجرح فكل وأطلق في قوله ولا بد من التسمية فشمل ما إذا كان المرمى إليه يحتاج إلى التسمية أو لا كالسمك، وقد شرط في الأول دون الثاني حتى لو رمى إلى السمك وترك التسمية عمداً فأصاب يحل أكله، فلو قال في صيد البر لكان أولى وسيأتي عن قاضيخان. ولا بد أن يكون المسمى يعقل التسمية فلا يؤكل صيد ومجنون إذا كانا لا يعقلان التسمية، أما إذا كانا يعقلانها أكل ويؤكل صيد الأخرس والكتابي لأن الملة تكفي عن التلفظ عند العجز. ولو سمى النصراني باسم المسيح لم يؤكل والصابئة إن أقروا بكتابي وإن يؤكل صيدهم وإلا فلا.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And tasmiyah at the time of release is necessary, and also wound in any part of its limbs). As for tasmiyah, due to the Almighty's saying: 'And do not eat of that upon which the name of Allah has not been mentioned' [al-An'am:121] and His saying, peace be upon him: 'So if you mention Allah over it and it wounds, then eat.' And he gave an absolute statement in saying 'tasmiyah is necessary', so it includes cases where the target requires tasmiyah or not, like fish. And it is conditioned in the former but not the latter, such that if one shoots at fish and deliberately omits tasmiyah and hits, its eating is permissible. So if he had said 'in land hunting' it would have been more appropriate, and it will come from Qadikhan. And the one who says the tasmiyah must be sane, so the hunt of an insane person who does not understand tasmiyah is not eaten; if they do understand it, it is eaten. The hunt of a mute and a Kitabi is eaten, because the millah (religious affiliation) suffices for utterance when unable. If a Christian says tasmiyah in the name of the Messiah, it is not eaten. The Sabians: if they acknowledge a Kitabi book, their hunt is eaten; otherwise, not.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the obligation of tasmiyah (saying Bismillah) when releasing a hunting animal. The text cites Quran and Hadith as evidence. It clarifies that tasmiyah is required for land hunting but not for fishing, as fish do not require slaughter. The person performing the release must be sane and capable of understanding tasmiyah; an insane person's hunt is not permissible. A mute and a Kitabi (People of the Book) are excepted because their religious affiliation suffices. A Christian saying tasmiyah in the name of Christ renders the prey impermissible. The passage also notes that the Sabians' hunt is permissible if they acknowledge a revealed book.

Key Terms
تسمية (tasmiyah): The act of saying 'Bismillah' (or similar invocation of Allah's name) when releasing a hunting animal.
صيد (sayd): Hunting; the act of pursuing and killing wild animals for food.
مجنون (majnun): An insane person; one who lacks sanity and may not understand tasmiyah.
كتابي (kitabi): A person of the Book (Jew or Christian) who follows a revealed Scripture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on eating fish caught by a hunter who deliberately omitted saying Bismillah?
A) The fish is haram because tasmiyah is always required.
B) The fish is halal because tasmiyah is not required for fish.
C) The fish is halal only if the hunter was forgetful.
D) The fish is haram unless the hunter is a Kitabi.

Key Takeaway
Tasmiyah is wajib at release for land hunting, with specific exceptions for fishing, those unable to speak, and People of the Book; deliberate omission makes the prey haram.

Is a Wound (Jarh) Required for Prey to Be Halal?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the necessity of a wound

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the requirement of a wound in hunting and explain the relied-upon position with its evidence.

Core Idea
A wound that releases flowing blood is required for prey to be halal, according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses a critical condition for the permissibility of hunted game: must the trained animal cause a wound that bleeds? While the Quran gives absolute permission, the Hanafi school, in its apparent narration, qualifies it by requiring a wound. However, a minority narration from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf says no wound is needed. We'll examine both sides and the reasoning for the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
The text presents a dispute within the Hanafi school. Locate the two positions: the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) requiring a wound, and the narration from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that does not require it.
The text also mentions al-Sha'bi as supporting the latter view.
2
Examine the proof for the non-requirement position
The opposing school cites the absolute Quranic verse (al-Ma'idah:4) 'So eat of what they catch for you' without restriction. Adding a wound would be adding to the text.
This is a pure argument from textual generality.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response from the apparent narration
The Hanafi position argues that the purpose is to extract flowing blood (دم مسفوح), which is normally achieved by a wound. If no wound, the animal becomes mawqudhah (beaten), which is explicitly prohibited. The absolute verse is interpreted in light of the beneficial wound, due to unity of the incident.
They also argue that if the absolute were left unrestricted, it would contradict the prohibition of mawqudhah.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a hunting dog kills by crushing or strangling without a wound, the prey is not halal according to the relied-upon view. If one follows the minority narration, it would be halal.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and its authority
The text states that the apparent narration is the relied-upon position. The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah, and the need to extract blood supports it.
This is the view adopted for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وظاهر عبارة المؤلف الاكتفاء بالجرح سالماً أولاً لكن قال في المحيط : إن جرحه لم يدمه اختلفوا فيه قيل لا يحل وقيل يحل، وقيل إن كانت الجراحة صغيرة لا يحل إذا لم يرم وإن كانت كبيرة يحل . وأما الجرح فالمذكور هنا ظاهر الرواية، وعن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف أنه لا يشترط ؛ رواه الحسن عنهما وهو قول الشعبي لقوله تعالى : فكلوا مما أمسكن عليكم [المائدة : ٤] مطلقاً من غير قيد بالجرح فمن شرطه فقد زاد على النص وهو نسخ ما عرف في موضعه، وكذا ما روينا من حديث عدي وثعلبة يدل على ذلك لأنه مطلق فيجري على إطلاقه وإلا لزم نسخة بالرأي وهو لا يجوز الظاهر قوله تعالى: ﴿وما علمتم من الجوارح وهو يشير إلى ما قلنا ولأن المقصود إخراج الدم المسفوح وهو يخرج بالجرح عادة ولا يختلف عنه إلا نادراً فأقيم الجرح مقامه كما في الذكاة الاختيارية والرمي بالسهم، ولأنه إذا لم يجرحه صار موقوذه وهي محرمة بالنص وما تلي ،مطلق وكذا ما روي فحملناه على المفيد لاتحاد الواقعة. وإنما لم يحمل المطلق على المقيد فيما إذا اختلفت الحوادث أو كان التقييد والإطلاق من جهة. السبب، وأما إذا كان من جهة الحكم والحادثة واحدة فيحمل عليه. ولو سمى حالة الإرسال فقتل الكل حلت ولو قتل الكل واحداً بعد واحد حل بخلاف ما إذا ذبح شاتين بتسمية فإنه لا يحل والفرق أن الحل في باب الصيد يحصل بالإرسال فتشترط التسمية وقت الإرسال والإرسال وجد وقت تسمية واحدة كما لو رمى سهماً إلى صيد فنفذ وأصاب صيداً آخر بخلاف ما لو ذبح شاة أخرى لأن الثانية صارت مذبوحة بفعل غير الأول فلا بد من تسمية أخرى، ولو اضجع شاتين وذبحها بتسمية واحدة حلا.
The apparent meaning of the author's statement is that a wound is sufficient, sound or not. But in al-Muhit it is said: If the wound does not cause bleeding, there is disagreement: some say it is not permissible, some say it is permissible, and some say if the wound is small it is not permissible if it does not throw, and if it is large it is permissible. As for the wound, what is mentioned here is the apparent narration. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that it is not required; al-Hasan narrated from them, and it is the saying of al-Sha'bi, due to the Almighty's saying: 'So eat of what they catch for you' [al-Ma'idah:4] absolutely, without restriction to wound. So whoever conditions it has added to the text, and that is abrogation as known in its place. Likewise, what we narrated from the hadith of Adi and Tha'labah indicates that, because it is absolute, so it applies absolutely; otherwise abrogation by opinion would occur, and that is not permissible. The apparent meaning of the Almighty's saying: 'And what you have taught of hunting animals' indicates what we said. And because the purpose is to extract the flowing blood, and it ordinarily exits through a wound, and rarely does otherwise, so the wound is established as its substitute, as in optional slaughter and shooting with an arrow. And because if it does not wound it, it becomes a beaten animal (mawqudhah), which is prohibited by text. And what was narrated, we interpret it as referring to the beneficial wound due to the unity of the incident. And the absolute is not carried upon the restricted when the events differ or the restriction and absoluteness come from different causes. But if they come from the same ruling and the event is one, then it is carried. If he says tasmiyah at the time of release and it kills all, they are permissible; if it kills them one by one, they are permissible, unlike if he slaughters two sheep with one tasmiyah, which is not permissible. The difference is that permissibility in hunting is achieved by release, so tasmiyah is required at the time of release, and the release occurs at the time of one tasmiyah, as if he shoots an arrow at game and it penetrates and hits another game. Unlike slaughtering another sheep, because the second becomes slaughtered by an action other than the first, so another tasmiyah is needed. And if he lays down two sheep and slaughters them with one tasmiyah, they are permissible.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the requirement of a wound for the prey to be lawful. The author's statement is interpreted as requiring a wound. However, al-Muhit reports a disagreement when the wound does not bleed. The apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) is that a wound is required, but there is a narration from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that a wound is not necessary, based on the absolute Quranic permission. The text argues that the purpose is to extract flowing blood, and a wound normally achieves that, so it is a substitute. However, if no wound occurs, the animal is considered beaten (mawqudhah), which is prohibited. The discussion concludes that if the wound is large enough to cause bleeding, it is sufficient; if not, there is disagreement. The text also addresses a related issue: if one tasmiyah is said at release and the animal kills multiple prey, all are lawful; but if one tasmiyah is said while slaughtering two sheep, only the first is lawful unless they are both laid down together.

Key Terms
جرح (jarh): A wound that causes blood to flow, inflicted by the hunting animal on the prey.
موقوذة (mawqudhah): An animal killed by a blow without a wound, which is prohibited in the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the status of a prey killed by a trained dog without any wound (e.g., by strangling)?
A) It is halal
B) It is haram
C) It is makruh
D) It depends on the intention

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi view requires a wound that extracts flowing blood for prey to be halal; if the animal kills without a wound, the prey is haram.

A Single Tasmiyah for Multiple Prey or Slaughter Animals
Ruling on the effect of a single tasmiyah on multiple animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a single tasmiyah at the time of release suffices for multiple prey, and distinguish it from slaughter where multiple acts require separate tasmiyah.

Core Idea
One tasmiyah at release covers multiple kills, but separate slaughter acts each need their own tasmiyah.

After discussing the wound condition, the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a practical scenario: if a hunter says tasmiyah once when releasing the animal, and it kills multiple game, are all halal? The answer is yes, in contrast to slaughtering two sheep with one tasmiyah, where only the first is halal unless both are laid down together. This lesson explains the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two cases: (a) a hunting animal released with one tasmiyah kills multiple prey sequentially; (b) a person slaughters two sheep with one tasmiyah.
Note the difference in the act that brings permissibility.
2
State the ruling for each case
For hunting: all prey are halal. For slaughter: only the first sheep is halal unless both are placed together for a single act of slaughter.
The text explicitly contrasts the two.
3
Understand the rationale
In hunting, permissibility is earned by the release (الإرسال), so the tasmiyah at that time covers all subsequent kills. In slaughter, each animal requires its own act (الذبح), so each act needs its own tasmiyah.
The comparison with shooting an arrow that hits multiple game reinforces this.
4
Apply to a variation
The text compares to an arrow shot at one game that hits another; both are halal with one tasmiyah at the shot.
This shows the principle extends to other hunting methods.
5
Derive the condition for a single tasmiyah to cover multiple
The unifying factor is that the act that makes the animal permissible (release for hunting, slaughter for slaughter) must be a single continuous action. If separate actions, separate tasmiyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وظاهر عبارة المؤلف الاكتفاء بالجرح سالماً أولاً لكن قال في المحيط : إن جرحه لم يدمه اختلفوا فيه قيل لا يحل وقيل يحل، وقيل إن كانت الجراحة صغيرة لا يحل إذا لم يرم وإن كانت كبيرة يحل . وأما الجرح فالمذكور هنا ظاهر الرواية، وعن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف أنه لا يشترط ؛ رواه الحسن عنهما وهو قول الشعبي لقوله تعالى : فكلوا مما أمسكن عليكم [المائدة : ٤] مطلقاً من غير قيد بالجرح فمن شرطه فقد زاد على النص وهو نسخ ما عرف في موضعه، وكذا ما روينا من حديث عدي وثعلبة يدل على ذلك لأنه مطلق فيجري على إطلاقه وإلا لزم نسخة بالرأي وهو لا يجوز الظاهر قوله تعالى: ﴿وما علمتم من الجوارح وهو يشير إلى ما قلنا ولأن المقصود إخراج الدم المسفوح وهو يخرج بالجرح عادة ولا يختلف عنه إلا نادراً فأقيم الجرح مقامه كما في الذكاة الاختيارية والرمي بالسهم، ولأنه إذا لم يجرحه صار موقوذه وهي محرمة بالنص وما تلي ،مطلق وكذا ما روي فحملناه على المفيد لاتحاد الواقعة. وإنما لم يحمل المطلق على المقيد فيما إذا اختلفت الحوادث أو كان التقييد والإطلاق من جهة. السبب، وأما إذا كان من جهة الحكم والحادثة واحدة فيحمل عليه. ولو سمى حالة الإرسال فقتل الكل حلت ولو قتل الكل واحداً بعد واحد حل بخلاف ما إذا ذبح شاتين بتسمية فإنه لا يحل والفرق أن الحل في باب الصيد يحصل بالإرسال فتشترط التسمية وقت الإرسال والإرسال وجد وقت تسمية واحدة كما لو رمى سهماً إلى صيد فنفذ وأصاب صيداً آخر بخلاف ما لو ذبح شاة أخرى لأن الثانية صارت مذبوحة بفعل غير الأول فلا بد من تسمية أخرى، ولو اضجع شاتين وذبحها بتسمية واحدة حلا.

When Dog or Leopard Eats from Prey: Hanafi Ruling
States the Hanafi ruling that if a dog or leopard eats from the prey, it is not halal, but if a hawk eats, it is halal, with inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a dog or leopard eats from the prey, contrast it with the Maliki/Shafi'i position, and cite the evidence for each.

Core Idea
If a dog eats from the prey, it is not halal – the animal caught for itself, not for you.

Hunting with trained animals is a classic fiqh topic with careful distinctions. The Hanafi school distinguishes between birds of prey and canines: if a hawk eats from the kill, the prey remains halal, but if a dog or leopard eats, it becomes haram. This ruling is contested by other schools, so we must examine the evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position clearly
What exactly does the Hanafi school rule when a dog, leopard, or hawk eats from the prey? Identify the three animals mentioned.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Which imams disagree, and what do they hold? Note that they equate all trained animals.
Malik and al-Shafi'i in his old opinion hold that even if the dog eats, the prey is halal.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
What is the primary evidence for the Hanafi position? Reference the hadith of Umar ibn Adi and the Quranic verse (5:3).
The hadith states: 'if the dog eats, do not eat, for I fear it caught for itself.'
4
Examine the opposing dalil
What proof do Malik and al-Shafi'i cite? The hadith of Abdullah ibn Tha'labah where the Prophet allowed eating even if the dog ate.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut the opposing evidence? They argue that the hadith of ibn Tha'labah is general and may be abrogated or restricted by the clearer prohibition.
The practical outcome (thamarah al-khilaf) is clear: Hanafis forbid, others permit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن أكل منه البازي أكل وإن أكل منه الكلب أو الفهد لا) وقال مالك والشافعي في القديم : يؤكل وإن أكل منه الكلب كالبازي لما روي عن عبد الله بن ثعلبة قال : يا رسول الله إن لي كلاباً مكلبة فأفتني في صيدها فقال : إن كانت لك كلاب مكلبة فكل ما أمسكت عليك الحديث إلى أن قال للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : وإن أكل منه؟ قال عليه الصلاة والسلام وإن أكل منه وفعل الكلب إنما صار ذكاة لعلمه وبالأكل لا فصار كالبازي. ولنا ما روينا من حديث عمر بن عدي وقوله تعالى: ﴿وما أكل السبع إلا ما ذكيتم [المائدة : ٣] وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام إذا أرسلت كلابك المعلمة وذكرت اسم الله تعالى فكل ما أمسكن عليك إلا أن يأكل الكلب فلا تأكل فإني أخاف أن يكون إنما أمسك على نفسه رواه البخاري ومسلم وعن ابن عباس أنه قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم «إذا أرسلت
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If the hawk eats from it, it is eaten; if the dog or leopard eats from it, it is not). Malik and al-Shafi'i in the old view said: it is eaten even if the dog eats from it, like the hawk, due to what was narrated from Abdullah ibn Tha'labah: he said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I have trained dogs, so give me a fatwa regarding their hunt.' He said: 'If you have trained dogs, then eat what they catch for you...' until he said to the Prophet: 'And if the dog eats from it?' He said, peace be upon him: 'And if it eats from it.' And the dog's action becomes a slaughter by its training, and eating does not [negate it], so it is like the hawk. Our evidence is what we narrated from the hadith of Umar ibn Adi and the Almighty's saying: 'And what the wild beast has eaten, except what you slaughter' [al-Ma'idah:3] and His saying, peace be upon him: 'When you send your trained dogs and mention Allah's name, eat what they catch for you, unless the dog eats from it, then do not eat, for I fear that it caught it for itself.' Narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. And from Ibn Abbas that he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'When you send...'
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the permissibility of hunted game when the hunting animal has eaten from it. The Hanafi ruling, stated by the author, is that if a hawk (بازي) eats from the prey, the prey is still halal, but if a dog or leopard (فهد) eats, it is not halal. Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i (in his old opinion) disagree, holding that even if the dog eats, the prey is halal, based on a hadith of Abdullah ibn Tha'labah. The Hanafi school responds with their own hadith evidence from Umar ibn Adi and the Quran [al-Ma'idah:3], along with a hadith from Bukhari and Muslim that explicitly prohibits eating from what a dog has eaten from, because it indicates the dog caught it for itself. The Hanafi position is that the dog's eating shows it was not trained to refrain, so it caught for its own sake, not for the hunter.

Key Terms
بازي (bazi): A type of hawk or falcon used for hunting; its eating does not affect permissibility.
فهد (fahd): Leopard or cheetah used for hunting; eating from prey makes it haram.
مكلبة (mukallaba): Trained dogs, specifically trained for hunting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a trained dog eats from the hunted prey?
A) The prey is halal
B) The prey is haram
C) It is makruh
D) It depends on how much it ate

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that if a dog or leopard eats from the prey, it is haram; if a hawk eats, it remains halal, based on explicit prophetic prohibition.

Condition of the Hunter's Understanding of Tasmiyah
Stating requirement of understanding tasmiyah for the hunter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that the hunter must understand the meaning of the tasmiyah and apply it to determine the permissibility of hunted meat for various categories (child, madman, mute, Kitabi, Christian, Sabian).

Core Idea
Hunted meat is permissible only if the hunter understands the tasmiyah, not merely utters it.

In this lesson, we examine a key condition for hunting: the person who sends the hunting animal (al-musamma) must understand the meaning of the tasmiyah. This understanding is essential for validity. The passage discusses exceptions and specific cases, including children, the insane, the mute, People of the Book, Christians who invoke Jesus, and Sabians.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its key condition
The passage states that the hunted meat is not eaten if the hunter (al-musamma) does not understand the tasmiyah. Understanding is the core condition.
2
Classify the categories mentioned
The passage divides hunters into: those who do not understand (child, madman) – invalid; those who do understand (same categories are valid if they understand); the mute and Kitabi – valid even without utterance; the Christian who says 'Bismil-Masih' – invalid; the Sabians – valid only if they acknowledge a revealed book.
3
Apply the condition to each category
For each category, determine whether the condition of understanding is met. If the hunter is sane and understands, the hunt is permissible unless an additional prohibition exists (e.g., Christian saying 'Bismil-Masih').
4
Distinguish between utterance and understanding
Note that the mute and Kitabi are excused from verbal utterance, but the condition of understanding is still implicitly met because their religion or ability to intend suffices. Utterance is not the goal; understanding is.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بد أن يكون المسمى يعقل التسمية فلا يؤكل صيد ومجنون إذا كانا لا يعقلان التسمية، أما إذا كانا يعقلانها أكل ويؤكل صيد الأخرس والكتابي لأن الملة تكفي عن التلفظ عند العجز. ولو سمى النصراني باسم المسيح لم يؤكل والصابئة إن أقروا بكتابي وإن يؤكل صيدهم وإلا فلا.
It is necessary that the one who names (al-musamma) understands the tasmiyah. So the hunting of a child and a madman is not eaten if they do not understand the tasmiyah. But if they understand it, it is eaten. And the hunting of a mute and a Kitabi (People of the Book) is eaten because their religion suffices for utterance when unable. If a Christian says the name of the Messiah (saying 'Bismil-Masih'), it is not eaten. As for the Sabians, if they acknowledge a Kitabi (revealed book) then their hunting is eaten, otherwise not.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage states the condition for the person who performs the hunting (the one who sends the dog or predator and says the tasmiyah). The Arabic term 'al-musamma' refers to the person who utters the tasmiyah. The condition is that he must be 'عاقل للتسمية' - he must understand the meaning of the tasmiyah. Therefore, if a child who does not understand, or an insane person, performs the hunting, their catch is not permissible, even if the words are uttered. However, if a child understands and intends, it is permissible. A mute person's hunting is permissible because Islam takes the place of verbal utterance when one is unable. Similarly, a Kitabi (Jew or Christian) may hunt and his catch is permissible even if he does not say the tasmiyah, because his religion suffices. But if a Christian says 'Bismil-Masih' (in the name of the Messiah), the catch is not permissible because it is not the name of Allah. The Sabians: if they acknowledge a revealed book (like the Psalms of David), then their hunting is permissible; otherwise, they are considered mushrikeen and their hunting is not permissible.

Key Terms
المسمى (al-musamma): The person who utters the tasmiyah when sending a hunting animal.
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): The utterance of 'Bismillah' at the time of sending the hunting animal.
الكتابي (al-kitabi): A Jew or Christian who follows a revealed scripture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the hunting of a madman (majnun) who does not understand the meaning of the tasmiyah?
A) It is permissible because he said the words.
B) It is not permissible because he does not understand the meaning.
C) It is permissible only if he is a Kitabi.
D) It is makruh tanzihi.

Key Takeaway
Understanding the meaning of the tasmiyah is a condition for the permissibility of hunted meat; utterance alone does not suffice.
